Advisory Board The Advisory Board is the consultative body of the Panama Canal Authority Board of Directors and senior management regarding the needs, requirements and improvements of the Canal’s international maritime service, in accordance with the Political Constitution of the Republic, the Canal Organic Law and its regulations. It is a forum composed of leaders from the international community who contribute with their opinions and experience to the design and improvement of the plans developed by the Administration for the future progress of the Canal. It is formed by 17 distinguished individuals from the maritime and business world who meet at least once a year when convened by the Board of Directors. The Advisory Board met once during fiscal year 2015, in Tokyo, Japan, on April 7 and 8. In the meeting the Administration presented performance updates on Canal operations, the Expansion Program’s progress and new projects. Ad-hoc Committee The Ad-hoc Committee was established by Law 28 of July 17, 2006, by which the proposal for construction of the Third Set of Locks was approved. The Committee’s role is to receive periodic progress reports on the contracting process and execution of the Panama Canal Expansion Program to analyze, evaluate, and make observations or recommendations that they consider pertinent. It is composed of seven Panamanian citizens that represent the following organizations: National Council of Organized Workers (CONATO), National Council of Private Enterprises, Chancellors Council, Civic Clubs, Ecumenical Committee, Executive Branch and National Assembly. To guarantee its commitment to transparency and accountability, the Panama Canal conducted four quarterly meetings and a field trip with the Ad-hoc Committee during fiscal year 2015. The committee From left to right: Jorge de la Guardia, Raúl Estripeaut, Juan Pablo Fábrega, Jorge L. members were thoroughly informed on the Expansion Quijano, Walter Smith, Marcos Allen y Juan Wong. Program’s progress. The meetings were chaired by the Minister for Canal Affairs and Chairman of the Board of Directors and were held on October 29, 2014, February 11, 2015, June 5, 2015 and September 24, 2015. The field trip to the construction sites of the new locks took place on June 5, 2015. Human Capital Labor Force The image of the Panama Canal synthesizes the identity of its people and projects a corporate culture and a unique national and international positioning. In the past year, the ACP has experienced great challenges which were overcome due to the talent and commitment of its human capital. The company is confident that the talent of each Canal worker is the key that enables the series of achievements for the benefit, development and progress of the country, to which we respond. The ACP workforce constitutes, without a doubt, the most important pillar of the waterway. The professionalism of the Canal worker, the management of human resources and equal opportunities based on a merit system remain the key to an organization of global excellence. Staffing In fiscal year 2015 the total workforce was composed of 7,837 permanent and 2,089 temporary workers, hired either for relief duty, specific projects or student development programs. A turnover rate of 4 percent, slightly higher than the rate for fiscal year 2014, confirms that the implementation of the Voluntary Retirement Incentive Program, facilitates mobility and generational change in the company. Panama Canal / ANNUAL REPORT 2015 139 The leadership program builds leaders, strengthens and hones skills, and develops talent in a more thorough way. During fiscal year 2015, 229 managers, supervisors and foremen and 96 leaders were trained in areas of personal leadership and strengthening of human resources knowledge. In addition, 99 participants completed mentoring training, giving them a unique opportunity to expand their own leadership experience through the use of skills that allow them to develop others by sharing their experience and providing support throughout the year. As part of the Succession Program, during fiscal year 2015, a pilot plan was implemented for critical positions in the vice presidencies offices. The process included the administration of diagnostic tests and interviews and the results permitted the Administrator and his immediate executive team to validate this process. During fiscal year 2015, a training program for pilots and tugboat captains was launched at the Center of Simulation, Research and Maritime Development (SIDMAR) which was updated with mathematical models integrating segments of the expanded Canal with the new locks, the navigation channels and the Culebra Cut. This is part of the Canal’s commitment to prepare its workforce to be capable of operating the Canal once the Expansion Program is completed. This program will intensify as the opening of the Third Set of Locks approaches. Technical development remains vital to ensure that the generational change in the craft-operational positions relies on a skilled and qualified workforce. The Panama Grows program, aimed at young people, and the Technical Journeymen Development and Upward Mobility programs, aimed at workers with some experience, have prepared 62 participants. Also, training in the maritime, industrial, and security areas resulted in 21,247 training instances. To strengthen the strategy of promoting a selfdevelopment culture, this year six new courses were offered in the ACP Corporate University Virtual Classroom. The topics included were: Leave Your Legacy, English for Specific Purposes, Preventing Domestic Risks, Effective Presentations, 140 Panama Canal / ANNUAL REPORT 2015 Preparation for Proficiency Tests, and Personal Finance. Performance Evaluation In fiscal year 2015 the consolidation of the individual performance evaluation cycle stood out for enhancing the continuous improvement of processes, the quality of the goals, and their alignment with business results. In this area, the ACP Performance Evaluation System covers 100 percent of the workforce, which allows the identification of the areas that require personalized development plans, with the corresponding follow-up so that employee performance is always directly related to the strategic focus of the company. Voluntary Retirement The ACP offers its workers the payment of a benefit when they retire upon reaching the age established by the Panama Social Security System (CSS). It was noted that at the end of fiscal year 2015, 76 percent of the workers accepted this benefit upon reaching the regular retirement age established by the CSS (57 years for women and 62 years for men), and 38 percent of the workers accepted this benefit upon reaching the early retirement age (55 years for women and 60 years for men). Panama Canal / ANNUAL REPORT 2015 143 Connectivity Incidence of the Panama Canal in the World, in the Context of Connectivity In general terms, when talking about the Panama Canal’s impact on the world, the focus is usually on the advantages it offers in transportation costs, the types of cargo, or the size of vessels transiting the waterway. However, the Canal has a global impact that goes beyond just the cost savings that it could represent within the transportation industry. Since its opening in 1914, the Panama Canal has had an extensive impact on the global community. The Canal has contributed to the development of many countries, offering them the capacity to increase their income by competitively transporting exports. These revenues allow countries to invest in projects to improve common welfare within their nations. The Canal has also benefited consumers, offering them the opportunity to obtain goods at more affordable prices. In addition to improvements in exports and consumer prices, studies on the Canal, its construction and the development of its conglomerate have significantly enriched the knowledge within the maritime world. The Canal is highlighted in many international conferences in areas such as energy, infrastructure and environment, and is a reference of transparency and social responsibility. The social benefits, which are usually not accounted for when measuring the influence of the Canal in the world, have a multiplier effect with a direct and an indirect impact on society. The social benefits are capable of creating additional economic and social impacts which are not easily observed, both at regional and local level. Considering the benefits to the world, the Canal should not only be measured based upon its commercial usefulness to the maritime transportation industry, but also by its importance as a strategic point for development. The Canal also has an impact on different global supply chains. In this sense, the waterway has been promoting the development of a business logistics hub, which will not only contribute to the development of Panama, but also at a regional and global level. This will be possible by taking full advantage of the basic benefits provided by the Canal’s connectivity. Approximately 14,000 vessels use the Canal every year, linking more than 1,700 ports in more than 160 countries. This activity has boosted investment in ports that are considered today to be the main Panama Canal / ANNUAL REPORT 2015 145 ports in container movement in Latin America. In addition, the Canal activity has promoted other activities, such as bunkering and container repairs, which have generated jobs and benefitted both our country and the users of these services. It is expected that all these benefits will grow once the Third Set of Locks begins operations. Moreover, the Panama Canal is conducting studies for new projects which include ports, bunkering services, transfer operations (Top-off), power generation and logistics parks. These projects will broaden the benefits to Panama and other regions, including benefits to markets in the United States, Asia, Europe and Latin America, by reducing logistics costs which will eventually transfer to consumers. Taking all this into account, the Canal is proud to say with certainty, that it will continue playing a significant role in global development in the centuries to come. Route Performance The Panama Canal registered 340.8 million PC/UMS 971 net tons during fiscal year 2015, a 4.3 percent increase from the previous fiscal year tonnage. Toll revenues amounted to B/.1.994 billion, a 4.4 percent increase from the prior fiscal year. Transits also increased 2.9 percent, from 13,481 in fiscal year 2014 to 13,874 in fiscal year 2015. From the perspective of market segments, container and bulk carriers lead the statistics with regard to transits. Since the dry bulk cargo is susceptible to weather-related factors, this segment usually shows greater variability. These segments were followed by chemical tankers, refrigerated cargo ships, car carriers and Ro-Ro, general cargo, oil tankers, gas carriers and passenger ships, 1 Panama Canal Universal Measurement System. 146 Panama Canal / ANNUAL REPORT 2015 TRANSITS BY MARKET SEGMENT Dry Bulk Container Chemical Tankers Refrigerated 2013 Vehicle Carriers/RoRo 2014 General Cargo 2015 Crude/Product Tankers Liquid-Gas Carriers Passengers Others 0 500 1,000 1,500 2,000 2,500 3,000 3,500 4,000 having slight variations from one year to the next, TRANSITS THROUGH THE PANAMA CANAL as shown in the graph. It is worth noting that the 14,000 13,874 transit of liquid bulk vessels (oil tankers, chemical 13,660 tankers and gas carriers ) are experiencing a boom 13,481 13,000 as a result of the discovery of new deposits of shale leading to an increase in exports from the 12,000 United States. 11,000 Fiscal year 2015 was characterized by a moderate economic growth in the United States and a 10,000 gradual slowdown in the rest of the world. 2013 2014 2015 Fiscal Year At the end of 2014 (fourth quarter) a relative improvement was observed in the United States, TOLLS the Eurozone and China, prompting optimistic (in billions of balboas) forecasts by the International Monetary Fund 1.994 (IMF), the Organization for Economic Cooperation 1.920 1.910 and Development (OECD) and other international 1.900 organizations. Nevertheless, these projections 1.880 showed a downward trend during the course of 1.860 the year as macroeconomic variables changed. 1.840 Significant events included a fall in the price of 1.850 1.820 raw materials such as oil, which lowered the 1.800 income of several major emerging markets, and a 2013 2014 2015 stronger value of the dollar relative to the Fiscal Year Panama Canal / ANNUAL REPORT 2015 147 currencies in these same markets. At the beginning of 2015, a cold wave similar to that of 2014 had an impact on the growth of the United States economy. The growth rate of retail, automobile and construction sales experienced significant declines; however, they improved after April and maintained an upward trend for the rest of the year. The continued rise of the dollar throughout this period had an effect on exports. Meanwhile, the United States Federal Reserve (known as the Fed), which had proposed an increase in interest rates in September forseeing an improvement in the US economy, decided to delay the increase in order to reduce the vulnerability posed by the weakness of other economies, particularly China and the Eurozone. Employment rates scored significant gains until July. Nonetheless, in August and September, employment estimates were much lower than expected by the Fed. The unemployment rate stood at 5.1 percent in August and September, the lowest since March 2008. The Eurozone economy had a slow but steady growth since October 2014. The recovery has been mixed, as Germany, Ireland and Spain have showed a relatively modest growth, while economic growth in France and Italy has lagged. A noteworthy development in the Eurozone during fiscal year 2015 was the negotiations involving the Greek sovereign debt. Negotiations between Greece and the rest of the Eurozone over austerity measures required for an agreement on the debt payment and its implementation caused much uncertainty and curtailed investment. Several international organizations, including the IMF, were greatly concerned about the possible impact of Greece exiting the Eurozone. In the end, Greece accepted the austerity measures and the levels of uncertainty faded. The economy in the Eurozone improved somewhat in August and September, but the threat of deflation remained significant for the rest of the year. Asian economies also experienced a slowdown. This situation was related to China’s economic slowdown, which reduced volumes of both its exports, due to weaker global demand, and its imports, as a result of production decreases in 148 Panama Canal / ANNUAL REPORT 2015 China. The Chinese government has tried to boost economic growth by keeping interest rates low, developing infrastructure and devaluing its currency, the renminbi. However, indicators show a clear economic slowdown, especially in terms of imports and consumption. During July and August, China’s stock markets experienced a correction of about 40 percent, which was estimated to be close to 4 billion dollars. This situation was of great concern for other international stock exchanges, but the fears of a possible contagion never materialized. Japan’s economy also experienced a slowdown. Despite capital injections as part of the Abenomics policy named after Prime Minister Shinto Abe, Japan’s economy has not taken off. The IMF has indicated that it is likely that acceptance and implementation of economic reforms in Japan has not been swift enough and that the Prime Minister should carry out his economic policies at a more rapid pace. Japan was one of the main countries that supported the signing of the Trans-Pacific Partnership (TPP), due to its need for increasing foreign trade, partly due to the weak flow of exports to China. Full Container Vessels Segment The full container vessels segment performed well during fiscal year 2015. A total of 3,067 full container ships transited the waterway, with a volume of 115.1 million PC/UMS tons, 12.0 million TEU2 capacity, and B/.945.4 million in toll revenues. These figures reflect an increase of 6.1 percent in transits, 3.7 percent in PC/UMS 97 tons, 4.0 percent in TEU capacity, and 3.7 percent in tolls relative to the previous fiscal year. Revenues from full container vessels represent 47.4 percent of all tolls collected by the Canal during fiscal year 2015. During fiscal year 2015, the increase of cargo through the Canal was due to the introduction of seven new liner services since January, five in the Asia-US East Coast route, one in the US West Coast-Europe route and one in the North-South route. The new services deployed in the Asia-US East Coast route resulted from the deviation of cargo from US West Coast ports caused by the delay in the contract renewal negotiation between the International Longshore and Warehouse Union (ILWU) and the Pacific Maritime Association (PMA). 2Acronym of Twenty-foot Equivalent Unit, which means Unit Equivalent to Twenty Feet. Panama Canal / ANNUAL REPORT 2015 149 Imports of containerized cargo at major ports on the US East Coast, the main region of origin and destination of containerized cargo through the Panama Canal, recorded consecutive increases throughout fiscal year 2015, which contributed to the growth of the volume of cargo passing through the waterway. With the introduction of new capacity through the Canal, shipping lines are preparing their bases and gathering their TEU quotas for the loyalty program included in the new toll proposal which will begin with the opening of the Third Set of Locks. The number of liner services through the Panama Canal varied considerably during 2015, ending the year with 33 services, which is an increase of four services over the previous year. However, the average vessel size decreased from 4,004 TEU in 2014 to 3,925 TEU at the end of fiscal year 2015, a two percent variation. Reefer Vessels Segment During fiscal year 2015, reefer vessels registered 963 transits through the Panama Canal, 8.8 million PC/UMS 97 tons, 99,527 TEU transported above deck, and B/.44.9 million in toll revenues. A shortfall of 36 transits compared to fiscal year 2014 caused a reduction of 3.6 percent in PC/UMS 97 tonnage. Nevertheless, an 11.7 percent increase of TEU transported above deck resulted in similar toll revenues as in fiscal year 2014, with a slight one percent decrease. Bananas remain the main commodity transported in reefer vessels through the Panama Canal, with 2.1 million long tons of bananas, accounting for 62.9 percent of the transported cargo. It should be noted that 82.3 percent of the transported bananas originated in the West Coast of South America. This segment faces three threats which are gradually decreasing its competitiveness: the shift 150 Panama Canal / ANNUAL REPORT 2015 of perishable cargo from conventional reefer vessels to refrigerated containers, the age of the fleet, and changes in trade patterns. In recent years, the migration of perishable cargo from specialized vessels to refrigerated containers has been increasing due to the guarantee they offer to preserve cargo temperature and their compatibility with the existing global intermodal transportation system. This situation, in addition to the current oversupply of containerships and the connectivity offered by liner services, are further disadvantages for conventional reefer vessels business. Likewise, the specialized reefer vessels capacity is expected to decline over the next five years due to the advanced age and the scrapping of its fleet. In contrast, the fleet of containerships is young and with an optimized capacity for refrigerated cargo. On the other hand, the demand in emerging key markets and a growing middle class like China, are the new market targets for South American producers, who have begun to diversify their export markets. The aforementioned threats will continue to negatively impact this market segment. Liquid Bulk Segment The Liquid Bulk Segment marked an all-time record in every traffic indicator. This segment registered 2,754 transits, 63.2 million PC/UMS 97 tons, and B/.291.8 million in toll revenues, which represents increases of 17, 23, and 21.7 percent in the number of transits, PC/UMS 97 tonnage and toll revenues, respectively, when compared to fiscal year 2014. This record was driven by an increase in the transits of laden and ballast vessels with beams 100 feet and over, which rose 27.8 percent relative to fiscal year 2014. The total cargo transported during fiscal 2015 also reached a historical record of 57.9 million long tons or 13.2 percent above fiscal year 2014, boosted by the transits of vessels with beams of 100 feet or more through the Panama Canal. Crude oil and petroleum product tankers recorded increases of 12 percent in transits, 17.2 percent in PC/UMS 97 tons and 15.7 percent in toll revenues due to the increase of 19.4 percent in transits Panama Canal / ANNUAL REPORT 2015 151 of tankers laden and in ballast with beams of 100 feet and over, when compared to fiscal year 2014. Cargo transported by tankers increased 8.4 percent over the previous fiscal year, from 17.5 million long tons of cargo in fiscal year 2014 to 18.9 million long tons in fiscal year 2015, where tankers with beams of 100 feet or more carried more than 98 percent of this type of cargo. Crude oil was the product with the highest volume carried by tanker vessels in fiscal year 2015, mainly in the Ecuador to Gulf of Mexico route, which grew by 6.9 percent compared with the previous fiscal year. Ecuadorian Napo and Oriente heavy crudes are in very high demand by United States refineries, as these types of crude are optimal for blending with light crudes extracted from shale oil deposits in the United States3 and are sold at a lesser price than WWT (West Texas Intermediate, the US crude of reference), creating strong incentives to import these types of crude by US refineries.4 Chemical carriers posted increases of 12.3, 16.8 and 15.9 percent in the number of transits, PC/UMS 97 tons and toll revenues, respectively, when compared to fiscal year 2014. This performance was due to a 24.8 percent increase in transits of chemical carriers laden and in ballast with beams of 100 feet and over. The cargo carried in chemical carriers increased 10.8 percent in fiscal year 2015 compared to fiscal year 2014, from 30.4 to 33.7 million long tons of cargo, where vessels with a beam range of 100 feet and over transported 77.1 percent of this cargo type. Petroleum products such as gasoline and diesel recorded the highest volumes transported through the Panama Canal, increasing 47.7 3Repsol, BP and Mitsubishi win tenders to buy Ecuador crudes, Reuters, November 2014. 4Impact of low crude prices on refining, McKinsey & Company, February 2015. 152 Panama Canal / ANNUAL REPORT 2015 and 10 percent, respectively, over the previous fiscal year. The main routes of petroleum products originated in the Gulf of Mexico bound to the West Coast of Central America (Mexico, Guatemala and El Salvador) and South America (Ecuador, Peru and Chile). Moreover, chemicals and petrochemicals such as benzene, xylene and toluene among others, showed an increase of 20.4 percent from the previous fiscal year. The main routes of chemicals originated in the Gulf of Mexico bound to Asia (Japan and South Korea) and vice versa. It should be noted that most of the petroleum products are transported in chemical/oil tanker vessels, while petrochemicals are transported in chemical tankers. Refineries in the Gulf of Mexico have experienced an increase in exports of petroleum products by processing record volumes and achieving high levels of utilization,5 positioning themselves as one of the most competitive refinery parks in the global market. This situation, coupled with current lower oil prices, has flooded Latin American markets and has benefited transits of chemical tankers carrying petroleum products through the Panama Canal on vessels with beams of 100 feet and over. On the other hand, the low cost of natural gas as feedstock for the production of chemicals in the United States has been an important driver in the industry and it is expected to close 2015 with an increase of 4.0 percent against 2014,6 benefiting the transits of chemical tankers through the Canal. Meanwhile, gas carriers registered excellent traffic indicators, with increases of 54 percent in the number of transits, 68.8 percent in PC/UMS 97 tons and 68.4 percent in toll revenues, compared to fiscal year 2014. This remarkable performance of gas carriers was driven by the increase in transits of vessels laden and in ballast with beams of 100 feet and over. Cargo transported on gas carriers through the Panama Canal during fiscal year 2015 showed an increase of 62.3 percent over fiscal year 2014, going from 3.2 to 5.2 million tons of cargo, driven by the increase in exports of propane and butane extracted from shale formations in the United States. 5Net petroleum product exports continue to increase, US Energy Information Administration, July 2015. 6Chemical Outlook 2015 By Region, Chemical and Engineering News, January 2015. Panama Canal / ANNUAL REPORT 2015 153 The growth in propane production in North America (United States and Canada) has triggered an increase in US exports of propane, butane (also known as liquefied petroleum gas or LPG) and ethane since 2010. United States exports of LPG and ethane have increased from around 55 thousand barrels per day in the mid-2000s to more than 700 hundred thousand barrels per day in the first four months of 2015. Most of these exports have been sent to international markets through the Targa and Enterprise export terminals in Houston bound to Panama, Guatemala, Chile, Ecuador, South Korea and China. In addition, the Pacific coast of Panama is used to perform ship-to-ship transfer operations (top-off) of LPG. The transfer operation is carried out using a VLGC-Panamax vessel loaded in Houston with LPG, which passes through the Panama Canal and transfers the cargo to a VLGC that is anchored in the Pacific. Once loaded, the VLGC begins its journey to Japan and China after which it returns to the Panamanian Pacific coast to repeat the operation. Dry Bulk Carrier Segment For the second consecutive year, dry bulk carriers posted the most transits through the Panama Canal. In fiscal year 2015, dry bulk carriers recorded a total of 3,263 transits, 82.9 million PC/UMS 97 tons and B/.401.4 million in toll revenues. While vessel admeasurement tonnage (PC/UMS 97) decreased 3.5 percent over fiscal year 2014, it was the fourth highest level in history. In a similar manner, toll revenues were the second highest ever recorded. Fiscal year 2015 continued to register very good levels of cargo shipments by dry bulkers. A total of 115 million long tons of cargo were recorded in fiscal year 2015, the highest reported level in 7Market Snapshot: Exports of North American Propane on the Rise, National Energy Board Canada, August 2015. 8Very Large Gas Carrier – Post-Panamax. 9Market Research, ACP Liquid Bulk Segment, September 2015. 154 Panama Canal / ANNUAL REPORT 2015 history. The percentage of loaded transits compared to total transits increased from 83.3 percent in fiscal year 2014 to 90.4 percent in fiscal year 2015. Shipments of grains, salt, iron and steel manufactures and ores were prominent. Grains, the main commodity group transported in dry bulk carriers, reached a new record with 51.3 million long tons, up 7.5 percent from 47.7 million long tons in fiscal year 2014. The main route of grains from ports in the US Gulf of Mexico bound to China, Japan and South Korea continued to strengthen with record flows of soybeans and sorghum. These grains are mainly used for processing animal feed. China has become a net importer of grains; imports from the United States through the Panama Canal have increased 13 percent annually, on average, over the past 5 years. Shipments of crude salt also surpassed the record level reached the previous year. In fiscal year 2015, salt shipments totaled 10.6 million long tons, an increase of 27.7 percent compared to the previous year. Salt purchases from the extensive salt flats in the Pacific coasts of Chile and Mexico remained strong. These shipments are driven by US East Coast cities needing to secure salt supplies to melt snow on roads, prompted by expectations of a severe winter. Other cargoes with record levels in fiscal year 2015 were manufactures of iron and steel and copper and zinc ores. Shipments of products of iron and steel totaled 12.5 million long tons, mainly due to higher inflows from Japan, South Korea and China to the east coasts of Mexico, the United States and South America. Shipments of copper ore from Chile and Peru to various European destinations recorded an all-time high of 2.0 million long tons. Zinc ore shipments totaled 1.5 million long tons, mainly in trade routes from Alaska, Chile and Peru to Europe. On the other hand, coal shipments totaled 10.1 million long tons, a decrease of 27.7 percent over the previous year. Thermal coal, mainly from the Caribbean coast of Colombia to Chile, has faced increased competition from other sources in Australia, Canada and the Riesco Mine in Southern Chile. Other declining cargoes were lumber products and petroleum coke. Panama Canal / ANNUAL REPORT 2015 155 Vehicle Carriers and Ro-Ro Segment In general, the vehicle carriers/Ro-Ro market segment had a strong performance during fiscal year 2015, where their Panama Canal traffic indicators showed positive results in comparison to the previous fiscal year. During fiscal year 2015, the segment recorded a total of 844 transits and 48.2 million PC/UMS 97 tons. Relative to fiscal year 2014, these figures represent a 3.6 percent increase in transits and a 5.2 percent increase in PC/UMS 97 tonnage. Vessels 100 feet and over in beam accounted for 94.5 percent of all transits. Toll revenues during 2015 were B/.201.4 million, a 5.4 percent increase over fiscal year 2014. This growth in revenues was due to an increase in traffic. Meanwhile, the level of freight transported by the Panama Canal increased compared with fiscal year 2014. Cargo tonnage totaled 4.9 million long tons, an 8.1 percent increase above fiscal year 2014, when 4.6 million long tons were transported via the Panama Canal. The increase in cargo volume was driven by exports from Japan, South Korea, Mexico, Germany and the United Kingdom to the US East and West coasts, driven by the strong demand of US consumers. The main trade route for the Panama Canal, Japan-US East Coast, posted 1.1 million long tons, an increase of 11.9 percent over the previous fiscal year. In turn, the Europe (Germany/United Kingdom/Belgium) route to the US West Coast registered 0.6 million long tons, an increase of 20,000 long tons compared with the same period during the previous year. The South Korea US East Coast route remained steady with 0.3 million long tons. The good performance recorded by this segment during fiscal year 2015 was mainly due to a turnaround in light vehicle sales in the US market, which in turn has driven export increases from Asia and Europe to the United States. 10Roll-on/roll-off. 156 Panama Canal / ANNUAL REPORT 2015 Meanwhile, Japan, currently the point of origin in the main route through the Canal, was not impacted this fiscal year by the regional production strategy, but rather benefited from vehicle sales in the United States and by the yen. However, Japan could be affected if the Fed implements a rise in interest rates. Passenger Vessels Segment During the 2014-2015 cruise season, the traffic of passenger vessels was lower than in the previous period. During fiscal year 2015, the segment registered 208 transits (171 full transits and 37 turnarounds), 10 transits less than the 218 transits during the previous year (178 full transits and 40 turnarounds). The total number of passengers was 206,171 or 12.2 percent less than the 234,865 registered during the previous fiscal year. Tolls revenues amounted to B/.37.1 million, 8.8 percent less than the B/.40.7 million recorded during fiscal year 2014. During fiscal year 2015, vessels charged per berth accounted for 85.2 percent of the total revenue of this segment. The Panama Canal registered 236,294 billable berths, a decrease in the order of 34,075 berths, or 12.6 percent, when compared to the 2014-2015 season. Conversely, vessels charged on a PC/UMS 97 basis this year accounted for 14.8 percent of the total revenue for the segment and 47.2 percent of the total transits, and a total of 1.3 million PC/UMS 97 tons (21.1 percent above the tonnage registered during the 2013-2014 cruise season). For cruise season 2014-2015, cruise lines such as Princess Cruises, Holland America Line, Celebrity Cruises and Norwegian Cruise Lines deployed their vessels to the Panama Canal, performing full and partial transits, originating mainly from US ports in Miami. In addition, two new ships made their maiden transits of the Panama Canal, the Europa 2 on January 20, 2015, and the Costa Atlantica on April 24, 2015. Canal executives and operation personnel presented Panama Canal Honorary Pilot Licenses to 11 retiring vessel masters in recognition of their long maritime service, in presence of representatives from their respective shipping agencies. In addition, 50 appreciation plaques were also given to vessels doing their inaugural transit. Dredging Services as Part of Operations During this period, the dredging components of the Culebra Cut straightening and Widening Project and the Gatun Lake Deepening Project Panama Canal / ANNUAL REPORT 2015 163 were completed, with the completion of 267 programmed deliverables. With regards to the project to widen Chagres Crossing and Gamboa Reach to 300 meters, 4.4 million cubic meters were dredged, achieving a project global progress of 57 percent. As part of the support to the Expansion Program, dredging works were performed on the south plug of the Atlantic Locks, the north plug of the Pacific Locks, and the gate dock area in the Pacific Locks. In addition, the pumping system used to fill the new Pacific Locks was installed and operated and the drilling and blasting Baru Barge was rented from contractor Jan De Nul for the removal of the south plug of the Pacific Locks. Operation Milestones Besides the historical tonnage record achieved this fiscal year, the Panama Canal also had historical records in other areas. For instance, the transit of 7,771 Panamax vessels exceeded by 392 ships the previous record set in fiscal year 2014 and the transit of 8,973 supers exceeded by 506 the previous record set in fiscal year 2014. Furthermore, 91 days with a million or more tons transited, exceeded by 15 days the previous record of 76 days set in fiscal year 2012. The eighth meeting of the ACP Maritime Navigation Advisory Board was held on August 17 20, 2015. During the meeting, the transit and lockage procedures for Neo Panamax4 vessels were validated, and training plans, progress of the ACP Scale Model Maneuvering Training Center, and chartering of a Neo Panamax vessel for on-site training were discussed. The Advisory Board was very pleased with the progress shown in preparation for the operations of the Third Set of Locks. In an effort to mitigate El Niño effects, water-saving initiatives were implemented, such as lockages with low equalization in Miraflores and Gatun Locks, and the utilization of intermediate miter gates (short-chamber lockages) in all three locks. Both initiatives represented daily savings of two lock chambers, which, in addition to the implementation of cross-filling of the lock chambers, represented daily savings of four chambers or 13 million gallons of water per day. Preparations for the Operation of the Third Set of Locks Significant progress was achieved in the preparation for the operation of the Third Set of Locks. Transit 4Vessels with dimensions greater than Panamax or Panamax Plus that comply with the size and draft limitations of the new locks: namely, 1200.48 feet (366 meters) in length by 160.72 feet (49 meters) in beam by 49.87 feet (15.2) TFW draft. 164 Panama Canal / ANNUAL REPORT 2015 scheduling software programs were modified to include restrictions that will apply to Neo Panamax vessels and improve the management of the resources such as the pilots, tugboats, and boarding personnel. Simulations of tugboat and launch assignments to operate the Third Set of Locks were completed. Operation procedures for tugboats, deckhands, and linehandlers were defined, as well as firefighting support for Cocoli and Agua Clara Locks, based on scheduling of vessels with hazardous cargo. Firefighters were also trained in anticipation of the transits of vessels transporting liquefied natural gas (LNG). New tariffs were established for transit-related services (tugboats and deckhands) and other marine services (bookings, PCSOPEP5 and piloting) required for the transit of Neo Panamax vessels. Training of pilots and tugboat captains continued in order for them to be familiarized with transit and lockage procedures of Neo Panamax vessels, including training sessions at the Simulation, Investigation and Maritime Development Center (SIDMAR), where they were exposed to simulation navigation of Neo Panamax vessels through the new channels and locks, including harbor movements. Upward mobility developmental programs for marine traffic controllers, harbor controllers, transit schedulers, port entry coordinators, admeasures and billing technicians were successfully completed. This process was done in order to ensure that qualified personnel will fill all key positions. Training in Neo Panamax vessels transit procedures began in order to familiarize all personnel involved in the process with the operation of the Third Set of Locks. In addition, the Terms of Reference were drafted for the chartering of a Neo Panamax vessel to conduct on-site training of all Canal personnel directly involved with the operation and transit of Neo Panamax vessels through the new locks. New Initiatives to Improve Service and Capacity In order to improve customer service, a new toll structure was implemented and admeasurement regulations were updated. This has facilitated 5Panama Canal Shipboard Oil Pollution Emergency Plan Panama Canal / ANNUAL REPORT 2015 165 responses to the many consultations and recommendations made by clients. The preparation of the new vessel reservation system also began, which considers both the needs of the Third Set of Locks and improvements identified throughout time. For the implementation of these new processes for vessel transit through the Third Set of Locks, training courses were offered to the personnel to ensure that, once the procedures are implemented, they can be managed without issues. In addition, Canal customers were offered courses in order to provide insight into these processes and use them easily and efficiently. An inter-institutional team was formed with representatives of Canal area ports, shipping agencies, and the ACP, to analyze harbor operations and its interaction with the Panama Canal, search for opportunities to improve transit operations and harbor movements, and optimize the use of the navigation channel to benefit all parties involved. New radars were acquired for Cristobal and Balboa signal stations, to improve accuracy when identifying the vessels arriving at Canal waters and their location. This will, in turn, improve the use of anchorage areas at Canal entrances. Additionally, a radar was acquired for Gatun Lake area, which will allow for better administration of the Gatun anchorage, especially when operations of the Third Set of Locks begins. The Canal acquired pilot portable units (PPU) to assist pilots during transits and harbor movements. This will enable a safer and faster operation, especially in the Third Set of Locks and during adverse weather conditions (rain and fog), improving the Canal’s capacity. Operational Infrastructure Maintenance The first phase of a dry chamber overhaul at Pedro Miguel Locks was completed and most of the contract to paint the gates was executed. To increase the reliability of the turntables at Pedro Miguel and Miraflores Locks, new propulsion systems were purchased. Additionally, repairs of tow tracks and 166 Panama Canal / ANNUAL REPORT 2015 maintenance of the gate components were performed in Miraflores Locks. In the Gatun Locks, repairs were done to the scouring under the concrete slab located at the northern part of the locks and to damaged components of the gates, in addition to rising the stem valves and cleaning the tow tracks. In addition, fairing was done on tugboats Teribe, Changuinola, Sajalices, Sixaola, Guia and Gorgona, work boats Snapper, Wahoo and Quail, cargo barges #217 and #218, welding barge #34, submersible line barge #901, and hopper barge #861. Lock gates #56 and #57 were overhauled and structures of gate #69 were repaired. Infrastructure Development The expansion of Paraiso Landing for tugboat and launches was completed, at a cost of B/. 2.8 million. This will improve the service to tugboats by keeping the equipment in a strategic location to assist Panamax and Neo Panamax vessels in a timely manner. In addition, improvements were made to the worker waiting area, which should have a positive impact on work environment. As part of the Culebra Cut Straightening and Widening Project, the installation of buoys and bank lights was completed. In the industrial area of the Dredging Division, buildings 34X (Marine Signaling and Mechanical Shop) and 34 (Electric Shop) were remodeled, at a total cost of B/.1.9 million. Finally, the ACP Scale Model Maneuvering Training Facility achieved an 88 percent global progress. Panama Canal / ANNUAL REPORT 2015 167 Canal Expansion The Final Stretch As one of the nation’s leading economic activities, the Panama Canal needed to be expanded to maintain its competitiveness and take advantage of the geographical position which has made Panama an international trade, transportation and logistics hub. This expanded capacity will also ensure the integral and sustainable growth of existing and new maritime activities in the country. Having begun eight years ago and with a 93.9 percent progress by the end of fiscal year 2015, the Panama Canal Expansion Program is coming to an end. With only six percent remaining, its inauguration is just a few months away. Everything that was envisioned in 2006, when the first efforts began, is becoming a reality. Over the past year, a significant progress of 13.8 percent was achieved, including the excavation of the 49 million cubic meters of dirt and rock to complete the new Pacific Access Channel and a 99 percent completion of the 51.9 million cubic meters estimated in the dredging of the navigational channels. In addition, 44.6 million cubic meters, of an estimated 48.7 million, were excavated and dredged for the new locks and 4.39 million cubic meters of structural concrete, from the required 4.44 million, were poured in the new locks. All these achievements were possible due to the efforts of more than 10,000 workers, who have worked for this huge undertaking. Locks The Panama Canal Expansion’s main efforts are focused on the construction of the new locks complexes at the Pacific and Atlantic entrances of the Panama Canal. Each new lock has three chambers, nine water-saving basins, a lateral filling and emptying system and a redundant system of eight rolling gates. The chambers measure 55 meters wide, 427 meters long and 18.3 meters deep, to allow for the safe transit of Neo Panamax vessels. In fiscal year 2015, significant achievements were made in the new locks project which clearly define its progress, such as the arrival of the last four gates, the transfer of the eight gates to the Pacific locks using the existing Canal, and the installation of all 16 gates in their recesses, as well as their operational mechanisms. In recent months, the filling of the Cocoli and Agua Clara Locks was successfully initiated and the installation of 32 culvert valves, eight equalization valves and 36 conductor valves was concluded, along with all the dry testing and 94 percent of the filtration testing. Panama Canal / ANNUAL REPORT 2015 169 DESIGN AND CONSTRUCTION OF THE THIRD SET OF LOCKS Dredging and excavation volumes actual vs programmed through September 2015 50 45 40 44.6 Mm3 Cummulative Volume (millions cubic meters) 35 30 25 20 15 10 5 0 Mar. 10 May. 10 Jul. 10 Sep. 10 Nov. 10 Jan. 11 Mar. 11 May. 11 Jul. 11 Sep. 11 Nov. 11 Jan. 12 Mar. 12 May. 12 Jul. 12 Sep. 12 Nov. 12 Jan. 13 Mar. 13 May. 13 Jul. 13 Sep. 13 Nov. 13 Jan. 14 Mar.14 May. 14 Jul. 14 Sep. 14 Nov. 14 Jan. 15 Mar. 15 May. 15 Jul. 15 Sep. 15 Original Planned Cummulative Actual Cummulative Feb 2014 Scheduled Cummulative Another main milestone was the completion of Borinquen dams 1W, 2W and 2E, which will contribute in managing the level of the expanded Canal’s new navigational channel. In addition, removal of the south plug (cofferdam) in the Pacific and north plug in the Atlantic was initiated to allow partial filling of both sites. Meanwhile, construction of the main concrete structures was practically completed at both complexes reaching a 99 percent progress, with a total volume of 4.39 million cubic meters. This construction included the approaching structures 170 Panama Canal / ANNUAL REPORT 2015 in both locks. Land filling of the rear side of the walls in both locks was another task completed during this period. With regard to the water-saving basins, the Atlantic site is 99 percent complete, while the Pacific site is 95.4 percent complete. As construction moves forward, so does the installation of the polyvinyl chloride coating on the basins, as well as construction of access roads to the three levels of basin structures. Construction of lock facilities on the Atlantic site has advanced significantly, with a total of 44 buildings completed or in progress, and only two buildings pending construction, which represents 67 percent of the total work. Meanwhile, on the Pacific site, only one of a total of 46 buildings is pending to begin construction, which represents a 69.5 percent progress. In August 2015, a water seepage was detected in one of the concrete sills of the new gates in the Pacific site. ACP is closely monitoring the reinforcement and repair work to ensure that the project will meet the quality requirements established in the contract. Grupo Unidos por el Canal (GUPC), who is responsible for the design and construction of the Third Set of Locks, is working on the concrete sills, both on the Atlantic and Pacific sites. The repair process consists of monitoring, analyzing, designing and working on each individual sill. Once they have been repaired, electromechanical testing of the locks’ emptying and filling system will resume. It should be noted that GUPC is responsible for all the costs incurred due to this repairs. Repairs are estimated to be completed by January 2016. GUPC has presented several claims related to different aspects of the project’s implementation, in which they request money, time, or both. The Third Set of Locks contract establishes a three-step mechanism to evaluate the contractor’s claims. The first step is through the ACP representative, the second through the Dispute Adjudication Board, and the last step would be International Arbitration. GUPC’s claims are at different stages in the process. The ACP, through internal and external lawyers, claims groups and experts in various areas, has worked throughout all the fiscal year to collect, evaluate and analyze the information necessary for the defense of these claims. For detailed information on this claims, please refer to the financial statements included in this report. At the end of fiscal year 2015, the contract for the design and construction of the new locks was 93 percent complete. Work is expected to be completed by the second quarter of 2016. Panama Canal / ANNUAL REPORT 2015 171 Pacific Access Channel Completing the Canal Expansion required the construction of a new 6.1 kilometer access channel to connect the new Pacific Locks with Culebra Cut. Three of the four phases needed for this project have been completed in previous fiscal years. The fourth phase registered a 97 percent progress, with 26.79 million cubic meters excavated by September 2015. The excavation works have been completed. The most complex component of the access channel is the construction of a rock watertight clay-core dam, Borinquen 1E, which will maintain the same water level as Gatun Lake. On September 14, the consortium responsible for this project, ICA-FCC-MECO, successfully began filling the access channel that unites Culebra Cut with the Third Set of Locks, which required the partial removal of the Pacific north plug. One of the most important milestones of this project was accomplished during fiscal year 2015: the dredging of Gatun Lake, with the removal of 25.16 million cubic meters of material. In addition, twentyfive new navigational beacons were installed along Gatun Lake and 635 bank lights were delivered, which will be installed on both Pacific and Atlantic sides, along with 44 additional navigation buoys. The Dredging Division was primarily responsible for the dredging at Gatun Lake, using historical dredges, such as the Mindi and the Rialto M. Christensen, built in 1943 and 1977, respectively, and modern dredges, such as the Quibian I and the Alberto Aleman Zubieta, procured by the Panama Canal during the last four years. The deepening projects mentioned included the contract work which concluded on the northern reaches of Gatun Lake by Dredging International and on the north entrance of the Pacific Access Channel by Jan De Nul N.V. Raising Gatun Lake’s Maximum Operating Level This component of the Expansion Program is aimed at increasing the water-storage capacity of Gatun Lake in order to ensure an adequate supply of water for human consumption and other needs, while allowing the transit of Neo Panamax vessels with maximum drafts in the expanded Canal. The project consists of raising the maximum operating level of Gatun Lake 45 centimeters, from 26.7 to 27.1 meters and it required the modification of existing Canal structures to withstand the higher water level, as well as modification or relocation of docks, homes and other private structures. Project Occupational Safety The follow-up of occupational safety and industrial hygiene continued to be focused on aspects of the contractors’ work, including advance planning of key tasks. Tasks included underwater diving, dredging, connection of high-voltage power lines, filtration tests of the locks’ mechanical equipment, raising personnel to suspension scaffolds and work platforms, and initial activities related to the dismantling and demobilization of the contractors’ equipment and industrial installations. Many milestones were celebrated during the year, some field events with participation of national and international public figures, along with Canal and contractor’s personnel. For instance, the arrival of the final shipment of gates and their transit to the Pacific site through the existing locks, the filling of the new locks and the new Pacific Access Channel, and the removal of the cofferdams were major milestones during fiscal year 2015. The top priority during these special events was to guarantee the safety of all participants. The Panama Canal higher management and GUPC held regular meetings to strengthen awareness on safety issues at the highest levels. Safety measures in the field were also strengthened by working side by side with the contractors, through safety audits and visits focused on prevention, coupled with training efforts to promote a safe work environment. All these efforts resulted in a reduction of the incident rate. Panama Canal / ANNUAL REPORT 2015 175 Environmental Management Panama Canal environmental protection specialists ensured that actions were taken to mitigate social and environmental impacts by closely monitoring the different ongoing projects of the Expansion Program. The mitigation actions established in the Environmental Impact Assessment Study and the approval permit by the Panama Environmental Ministry were enforced. These actions include monitoring the quality of water, air and noise, managing solid and hazardous waste management in work areas, controlling sanitary conditions, erosion, sediment migration, secondary containment for fuels and lubricant storage protection, care and protections of fauna, and ecological compensation, among others. The Expansion Program Reforestation Program continue through the creation of new areas and maintaining existing ones. This program is conducted jointly with Panama’s Environmental Ministry and the Panama Aquatic Resources Authority in the provinces of Panama, Colon, Cocle, Herrera and Chiriqui. Two new reforestation contracts were awarded in the Madugandi Reservation and in Arimai covering 42 and 83 hectares, respectively, in the Darien province. These new sections increase the total reforested area to 937 hectares, out of 1,370 hectares required to complete the environmental compensation under the Expansion Program. The five-year maintenance phase for reforestation projects at the Center for Forestry Investigation (CIFO) phase II and El Montuoso Forest Reserve were completed this year, for a total of 100 hectares reforested this fiscal year. 176 Panama Canal / ANNUAL REPORT 2015 REFORESTATION PROGRAM LOCATION MAP 8 9 11 12 13 7 1 5 6 2 10 3 4 1. Camino de Cruces National Park -115 has During this period, the independent environmental contractor, Environmental Resources Management, certified that the Expansion Program is in compliance with all the mitigation requirements established in the environmental impact assessment and is aligned with the Ecuador Principles and the International Financial Corporation’s Performance Standards. As part of the Expansion Program, the Panama Canal also evaluates the impact to cultural resources in the project. During 2015, several archaeological findings associated with the Panama’s Departmental Panama Canal / ANNUAL REPORT 2015 177 and Republican historical periods were recovered during the inspections. One of the inspections took place in the former town of Gatun, as part of the channel widening project at Gorgona South. Several items were recovered at this site, mainly glass bottles, pottery and ceramic pieces of the Colonial Period and the French and United States Canal Construction Periods from 1880 to 1914. Several remains of columns foundations or bases of the buildings that existed in Gorgona were recorded, including two massive concrete and steel columns that may have been part of the YMCA Club House. During the fourth phase of the dry excavation of the Pacific Access Channel, an iron anchor and a metal vase were discovered. These were remnants of a ship with riveted parts, possibly used during the French Canal Construction Period. The ship was in very poor condition, however, the anchor was in good shape. Furthermore, the Director of the Historical Heritage National Directorate of the National Culture Institute (INAC) visited the facilities where the ACP stores the archeological findings that have been recovered as part of the Expansion Program. The Panama Canal will remain the temporary custodian of these items until the INAC determines how they will be handled. It should be noted that there has been a marked reduction in archaeological findings due to the near completion of the project and new areas with possible remains have not been excavated. Nevertheless, the monitoring activities continue in order to recover and preserve any finding that may appear during the final completion works of the project. Lectures and presentations on the Program’s progress have been presented to approximately 30,000 people at international and local level. As part of the information effort, massive public visits to the locks project were conducted and approximately 65,000 persons had the opportunity to tour the new locks before the chambers were flooded. The communities where informed about the procedure to cross from one side to the other, driving over the gates of the new locks. In order to promote the Expansion, the Panama Canal participated in a photography contest organized by the Engineering News-Record magazine in which two of the project’s photos were recognized. Furthermore, the Panama Canal organized and promoted the sale of 250 serigraph paintings by five renowned Panamanian artists, selected from the Expansion Program Art Collection. Panama Canal / ANNUAL REPORT 2015 179 Social and Environmental Commitment Corporate Social Responsibility and Communications Corporate Social Responsability The Panama Canal joined the Global Compact 13 years ago, with the firm intention to continuously improve its business practices for the benefit of Panamanians and all its stakeholders: the State, workers, customers, communities, and suppliers, in addition to the planet. At the beginning of a new century of service to the world, the Panama Canal has consolidated its management model in accordance with the principles of Corporate Social Responsibility (CSR): • Accountability: It is accountable and takes responsibility for its impact on society, economy, and environment. • Transparency: It is transparent on decisions and activities that influence its environment (economic, social, political, and ecological). It reveals clear, precise, and complete information on the policies, decisions and activities for which it is responsible to society; including known or probable impacts of business over their environment. • Ethical Behavior: It stands by ethical behavior, based on corporate values (reliability, honesty, loyalty, transparency, accountability, competitiveness), and does not tolerate corruption. • Respect the Rights and Interests of Stakeholders: It respects, gives due consideration, and responds appropriately and reasonably to the rights and legitimate interests of its stakeholders. • Respect for the Principle of National and International Law: It fully complies with laws and regulations at national and international level. • Respect for Human Rights: It respects human rights, and recognizes their role in corporate governance in general, as well as in relations with the stakeholders in particular. Crucial progress was made this year in terms of CSR. A comprehensive list of responsible practices throughout the company was completed and a new CSR strategy 2016-2020 was designed. This made possible the establishment of new initiatives to drive economic development, improve environmental performance and enhance human development. This new framework is focused on improving risks control, identifying new business opportunities, enhancing relationships with stakeholders, strengthening the company’s reputation, and improving 182 Panama Canal / ANNUAL REPORT 2015 Drive Improve Promote economic environmental human development performance development 1. In addition, the Canal launched a new television channel to offer up-to-date information on the waterway. During fiscal year 2015, the Panama Canal conducted a social perception study that showed that 82 percent of the population qualifies the Panama Canal as a good institution; 84 percent believe that the management of Canal Expansion Program is adequate; and 92 percent feel great pride in the Canal and consider it as part of the national identity.
